## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The relationship encodes Newton's second law with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and potential external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (combined damping mechanisms)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, indicating a symmetric potential well
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection; sign determines damping vs anti-damping
- Products of x┬▓ and v (like x┬▓┬Ęv) indicate amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c┬Ęt) or cos(c┬Ęt) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or exchanged through x,v-dependent terms
- Even powers of x in restoring force (x┬▓, xŌü┤) break spatial symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Cubic velocity terms (v┬│) combined with linear velocity terms can model Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c┬Ęx) indicate a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum dynamics rather than polynomial spring)
